### [1] [LCM: Lossless Context Management](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04050)
*Clint Ehrlich,Theodore Blackman*

Main category: cs.AI

TL;DR: Lossless Context Management (LCM) is a deterministic architecture for LLM memory that outperforms Claude Code on long-context tasks by using recursive context compression and task partitioning.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Current LLM memory architectures struggle with long-context tasks, and frontier coding agents like Claude Code with native file-system access represent a significant challenge. The authors aim to develop a more effective deterministic memory architecture that can outperform these advanced systems while maintaining lossless retrievability.

Method: LCM decomposes symbolic recursion into two deterministic mechanisms: 1) recursive context compression using hierarchical summary DAGs that automatically compact older messages while retaining lossless pointers, and 2) recursive task partitioning using engine-managed parallel primitives like LLM-Map to replace model-written loops. This represents a shift analogous to moving from GOTO to structured control flow in programming.

Result: The LCM-augmented coding agent Volt achieves higher scores than Claude Code on the OOLONG long-context evaluation, including at every context length between 32K and 1M tokens. The results demonstrate that recursive context manipulation can outperform not just conventional LLMs, but also frontier coding agents with native file-system access.

Conclusion: LCM represents both a vindication and extension of the recursive paradigm pioneered by Recursive Language Models. By trading maximal flexibility for termination guarantees, zero-cost continuity on short tasks, and lossless retrievability of all prior state, LCM provides a superior deterministic architecture for LLM memory in long-context scenarios.

Abstract: We introduce Lossless Context Management (LCM), a deterministic architecture for LLM memory that outperforms Claude Code on long-context tasks. When benchmarked using Opus 4.6, our LCM-augmented coding agent, Volt, achieves higher scores than Claude Code on the OOLONG long-context eval, including at every context length between 32K and 1M tokens.
  LCM may be considered both a vindication and extension of the recursive paradigm pioneered by Recursive Language Models (RLMs). Our results demonstrate that recursive context manipulation can outperform not just conventional LLMs, but frontier coding agents with native file-system access.
  LCM departs from RLM by decomposing symbolic recursion into two deterministic, engine-managed mechanisms: recursive context compression, in which a hierarchical summary DAG automatically compacts older messages while retaining lossless pointers to every original; and recursive task partitioning, in which engine-managed parallel primitives like LLM-Map replace model-written loops. This trade-off, analogous to the move from GOTO to structured control flow in program-ming language design, sacrifices maximal flexibility for termination guarantees, zero-cost continuity on short tasks, and lossless retrievability of all prior state.

</details>


### [2] [Regularized Centered Emphatic Temporal Difference Learning](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04100)
*Xingguo Chen,Chaohui Wu,Jinguo Ye,Chao Li,Shangdong Yang,Guang Yang,Tianyu Liang,Wenhao Wang*

Main category: cs.AI

TL;DR: RETD (Regularized Emphatic Temporal-Difference Learning) addresses stability-variance tradeoff in off-policy TD learning by regularizing centered emphatic updates while preserving favorable projection geometry.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Off-policy TD learning faces a structural tradeoff between stability, projection geometry, and variance control. While Emphatic TD (ETD) improves projection geometry through follow-on emphasis, it suffers from high variance in follow-on traces. The paper aims to address this tradeoff through Bellman-error centering while maintaining stability.

Method: Proposes RETD which applies Bellman-error centering to emphatic TD learning, but adds regularization to the auxiliary centering recursion. Specifically preserves the follow-on trace while regularizing only the centering part, corresponding to lifting the lower-right block of the coupled key matrix from 1 to 1+c (where c is regularization parameter).

Result: Theoretical analysis shows RETD preserves emphatic geometry and avoids instability of naive centered emphatic learning. Experiments on diagnostic linear off-policy prediction tasks demonstrate RETD maintains stability, preserves favorable geometry, and exhibits a robust intermediate regime for regularization parameter c across various diagnostics.

Conclusion: RETD successfully addresses the stability-variance tradeoff in off-policy TD learning by combining Bellman-error centering with careful regularization, providing a stable method that maintains the beneficial projection geometry of emphatic TD while controlling variance through regularization.

Abstract: Off-policy temporal-difference (TD) learning with function approximation faces a structural tradeoff among stability, projection geometry, and variance control. Emphatic TD (ETD) improves the off-policy projection geometry through follow-on emphasis, but the follow-on trace can have high variance. We revisit this tradeoff through Bellman-error centering. Although centering naturally removes a common drift term from TD errors, we show that a naive centered emphatic extension introduces an auxiliary coupling that can destroy the positive-definiteness of the ETD key matrix. We propose \emph{Regularized Emphatic Temporal-Difference Learning} (RETD), which preserves the follow-on trace and regularizes only the auxiliary centering recursion, corresponding to lifting the lower-right block of the coupled key matrix from \(1\) to \(1+c\). We derive the RETD core matrix, prove convergence under a conservative sufficient regularization condition, and evaluate the method on diagnostic linear off-policy prediction tasks. The experiments show that RETD avoids the instability of naive centered emphatic learning, preserves favorable emphatic geometry, and exhibits a robust intermediate regime for the regularization parameter \(c\) across the diagnostics.

</details>


### [3] [Actionable Real-Time Modeling of Surgical Team Dynamics via Time-Expanded Interaction Graphs](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04169)
*Vincenzo Marco De Luca,Antonio Longa,Giovanna Varni,Andrea Passerini*

Main category: cs.AI

TL;DR: This paper proposes a real-time approach for modeling surgical team dynamics using time-expanded interaction graphs to predict procedural efficiency and provide actionable insights for improving team performance.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Current surgical AI systems mainly focus on visual workflow signals but lack structured representations of intraoperative team interactions over time, despite team performance being crucial for surgical outcomes. There's a need for models that capture the complex interactions between technical execution and non-technical skills like communication and coordination.

Method: The authors use time-expanded interaction graphs where team members are modeled as time-indexed nodes and communication exchanges as directed edges. This spatio-temporal expansion enables dynamic interaction modeling while allowing efficient inference with a static graph neural network. The model predicts procedural efficiency as deviation from expected duration and supports real-time deployment.

Result: Experiments on recorded surgical procedures show that structured modeling of team interactions improves early identification of prolonged interventions and provides coherent, actionable explanations. The model successfully predicts procedural efficiency and supports counterfactual analysis to identify minimal communication changes for improved outcomes.

Conclusion: This work advances surgical AI toward real-time, team-aware, and actionable decision support in the operating room by providing a structured approach to model team dynamics, predict procedural efficiency, and offer interpretable behavioral insights for performance improvement.

Abstract: Surgical team performance arises from complex interactions between technical execution and non-technical skills, including communication and coordination dynamics. However, current surgical AI systems predominantly model visual workflow signals, lacking structured representations of intraoperative team interactions over time. We propose a real-time actionable approach for modeling surgical team dynamics using time-expanded interaction graphs, where team members are modeled as time-indexed nodes and communication exchanges define directed edges. This spatio-temporal expansion enables dynamic interaction modeling, while allowing efficient inference with a static graph neural network. The model predicts procedural efficiency as the deviation from the expected duration and supports real-time deployment. Beyond prediction, we perform a counterfactual analysis to identify minimal changes in communication structure and interpretable behavioral variables associated with improved predicted outcomes. Experiments on recorded surgical procedures show that structured modeling of team interactions improves early identification of prolonged interventions and provides coherent, actionable explanations. This work advances surgical AI toward real-time, team-aware, and actionable decision support in the operating room.

</details>


### [4] [ANDRE: An Attention-based Neuro-symbolic Differentiable Rule Extractor](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04193)
*Iman Sharifi,Peng Wei,Saber Fallah*

Main category: cs.AI

TL;DR: ANDRE is a novel differentiable ILP framework that uses attention-based logical operators to learn first-order logic programs from probabilistic data, overcoming limitations of both classical and existing neuro-symbolic approaches.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Current ILP approaches have significant limitations: classical ILP relies on discrete combinatorial search and is brittle under uncertainty, while differentiable ILP methods depend on predefined rule templates or inaccurate fuzzy operators that suffer from vanishing gradients or poor logical approximation in probabilistic settings.

Method: ANDRE uses attention-based logical operators to replace both rule templates and traditional logical operators with fully differentiable, attention-driven conjunction and disjunction operators that approximate logical min-max semantics. It enables flexible rule induction by softly selecting, negating, or excluding predicates within each rule while preserving symbolic structure.

Result: Extensive experiments on classical ILP benchmarks, large-scale knowledge bases, and synthetic datasets show ANDRE achieves competitive or superior predictive performance while reliably recovering correct symbolic rules under uncertainty. It remains robust to moderate label noise and substantially outperforms existing differentiable ILP methods in both rule extraction quality and stability.

Conclusion: ANDRE successfully bridges the gap between scalable differentiable learning and interpretable symbolic reasoning by providing an attention-based neuro-symbolic framework that can handle noisy, probabilistic data while maintaining the interpretability and structure of first-order logic programs.

Abstract: Inductive Logic Programming (ILP) aims to learn interpretable first-order rules from data, but existing symbolic and neuro-symbolic approaches struggle to scale to noisy and probabilistic settings. Classical ILP relies on discrete combinatorial rule search and is brittle under uncertainty, while differentiable ILP methods typically depend on predefined rule templates or inaccurate fuzzy operators that suffer from vanishing gradients or poor approximation of logical structure when reasoning over probabilistic predicate valuations. This paper proposes an Attention-based Neuro-symbolic Differentiable Rule Extractor (ANDRE), a novel ILP framework that learns first-order logic programs by optimizing over a continuous rule space with attention-based logical operators. ANDRE replaces both rule templates and logical operators with fully differentiable, attention-driven conjunction and disjunction operators that approximate logical min-max semantics, enabling accurate, stable, and interpretable reasoning over probabilistic data. By softly selecting, negating, or excluding predicates within each rule, ANDRE supports flexible rule induction while preserving symbolic structure. Extensive experiments on classical ILP benchmarks, large-scale knowledge bases, and synthetic datasets with probabilistic predicates and noisy supervision demonstrate that ANDRE achieves competitive or superior predictive performance while reliably recovering correct symbolic rules under uncertainty. In particular, ANDRE remains robust to moderate label noise, substantially outperforming existing differentiable ILP methods in both rule extraction quality and stability.

</details>


### [5] [Pro$^2$Assist: Continuous Step-Aware Proactive Assistance with Multimodal Egocentric Perception for Long-Horizon Procedural Tasks](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04227)
*Lilin Xu,Bufang Yang,Siyang Jiang,Kaiwei Liu,Kaiyuan Hou,Yuang Fan,Hongkai Chen,Zhenyu Yan,Xiaofan Jiang*

Main category: cs.AI

TL;DR: Pro$^2$Assist is a proactive AR assistant that continuously tracks task progress and provides timely assistance for long-horizon procedural tasks using multimodal sensing and step-aware reasoning.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Existing AI assistants are primarily reactive (responding to user queries) or provide limited proactive assistance only for isolated short-term events, lacking capabilities for continuous, step-aware support in long-horizon procedural tasks that involve multiple ordered steps.

Method: Pro$^2$Assist uses AR glasses for multimodal motion-based perception, extracts step-oriented procedural context from multi-scale temporal dynamics and expert knowledge, performs continuous reasoning to infer user needs, and displays timely assistance on AR glasses.

Result: The system outperforms best-performing baselines by over 21% in procedural action understanding accuracy and achieves up to 2.29x better proactive timing accuracy. A user study with 20 participants showed 90% find it useful.

Conclusion: Pro$^2$Assist demonstrates effective real-world procedural assistance by combining multimodal sensing, step-aware procedural context extraction, and continuous reasoning to provide timely proactive support for long-horizon tasks.

Abstract: Procedural tasks with multiple ordered steps are ubiquitous in daily life. Recent advances in multimodal large language models (MLLMs) have enabled personal assistants that support daily activities. However, existing systems primarily provide reactive guidance triggered by user queries, or limited proactive assistance for isolated short-term events rather than long-horizon procedural tasks. In this work, we introduce Pro$^2$Assist, a step-aware proactive assistant that continuously tracks fine-grained task progress and reasons over the user's evolving state to provide timely assistance throughout tasks. Pro$^2$Assist leverages multimodal data from augmented reality (AR) glasses to achieve motion-based perception. It then extracts step-oriented procedural context from multi-scale temporal dynamics and task-specific expert knowledge. Based on both sensory input and procedural context, Pro$^2$Assist performs continuous reasoning to infer user needs and display timely assistance on AR glasses. We evaluate Pro$^2$Assist using a dataset curated from public sources and a real-world dataset collected on our testbed with AR glasses. Extensive evaluations show that Pro$^2$Assist outperforms the best-performing baselines by over 21% in procedural action understanding accuracy, and it achieves up to 2.29x the proactive timing accuracy of baselines. A user study with 20 participants further shows that 90% find Pro$^2$Assist useful, indicating its effectiveness for real-world procedural assistance.

</details>


### [6] [Temporal Reasoning Is Not the Bottleneck: A Probabilistic Inconsistency Framework for Neuro-Symbolic QA](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04243)
*Tran Quang Liem*

Main category: cs.AI

TL;DR: A neuro-symbolic framework with Probabilistic Inconsistency Signal (PIS) that addresses LLM failures in temporal reasoning by separating representation extraction from symbolic reasoning, achieving perfect accuracy when given correct event graphs.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The paper challenges the prevailing belief that LLMs fail at temporal reasoning due to autoregressive logical deduction deficits. Instead, it identifies the root cause as unstructured text-to-event representation failures, where LLMs struggle to extract proper structural representations from text for temporal reasoning.

Method: The authors introduce a neuro-symbolic QA framework that lifts unstructured text into explicit event graphs and interval constraints, strictly decoupling semantic extraction from symbolic reasoning. The core innovation is a Probabilistic Inconsistency Signal (PIS) that unifies symbolic credal intervals with epistemic neural uncertainty via Evidential Deep Learning on LLM hidden states to detect structural breaks and isolate perceptual errors from reasoning failures.

Result: When provided with correct structural representations, the system achieves perfect 1.0 accuracy (4000/4000) with zero false positives/negatives on temporal arithmetic benchmarks. In broader noise-injected QA settings, it maintains 75.1% accuracy while enabling deterministic, step-level failure localization. The framework demonstrates that temporal reasoning itself isn't the bottleneck when proper structural representations are available.

Conclusion: The work reframes temporal QA from an algorithmic reasoning challenge to a structural alignment problem. By isolating the representation bottleneck from the reasoning substrate, it provides a verifiable path forward for reliable neuro-symbolic AI, showing that the fundamental issue isn't reasoning capability but rather proper structural representation extraction from unstructured text.

Abstract: Despite significant advances, large language models (LLMs) continue to exhibit brittle performance on complex temporal reasoning tasks. This failure mode is widely attributed to inherent deficits in autoregressive logical deduction. In this paper, we challenge this prevailing narrative, demonstrating that temporal reasoning is not the fundamental bottleneck; rather, the locus of failure lies in unstructured text-to-event representation. We introduce a novel neuro-symbolic question-answering framework governed by a Probabilistic Inconsistency Signal (PIS) that explicitly isolates perceptual errors from reasoning failures. By lifting unstructured text into explicit event graphs and interval constraints, our architecture strictly decouples semantic extraction from a symbolic reasoning engine. To robustly detect structural breaks, the PIS elegantly unifies symbolic credal intervals with epistemic neural uncertainty extracted via Evidential Deep Learning on LLM hidden states. Empirical evaluations reveal a striking paradigm shift: when provided with correct structural representations, our system's explicit proof traces achieve perfect 1.0 accuracy (4000/4000) and strictly zero false positives/negatives on temporal arithmetic benchmarks. On broader, noise-injected QA settings, the framework maintains a competitive 75.1\% accuracy while enabling deterministic, step-level failure localization. Ultimately, by isolating the representation bottleneck from the reasoning substrate, this work reframes temporal QA from an algorithmic reasoning challenge to a structural alignment problem, charting a verifiable path forward for reliable neuro-symbolic AI.

</details>


### [7] [Parallel Prefix Verification for Speculative Generation](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04263)
*Yuncheng Yao,Yuxuan Xia,Shengjie Wang,Danyang Zhuo*

Main category: cs.AI

TL;DR: PARSE introduces parallel semantic-level verification for speculative LLM inference, achieving 1.25-4.3× speedups by evaluating multiple draft prefixes simultaneously instead of sequential token-level verification.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Existing speculative decoding methods are limited by token-level verification, which leads to short acceptance lengths and modest speedups. While semantic-level verification could increase acceptance granularity, prior approaches require sequential verification that introduces significant overhead and limits practical gains.

Method: PARSE uses parallel prefix verification where the target model evaluates correctness across multiple draft prefixes in a single forward pass using a custom attention mask. This allows direct identification of the maximal valid prefix without sequential segment verification, making verification compute-efficient. The approach is orthogonal to token-level speculative decoding and can be composed with existing methods.

Result: PARSE delivers 1.25× to 4.3× throughput gain over the target model alone, and 1.6× to 4.5× when composed with EAGLE-3, across various models and benchmarks, with negligible accuracy degradation.

Conclusion: Parallel prefix verification represents an effective, general approach to accelerating LLM inference by moving from token-level to semantic-level verification while eliminating sequential overhead, with the method being composable with existing speculative decoding techniques.

Abstract: We introduce PARSE (PArallel pRefix Speculative Engine), a speculative generation framework that accelerates large language model (LLM) inference by parallelizing prefix verification on a semantic level. Existing speculative decoding methods are fundamentally limited by token-level equivalence: the target model must verify each token, leading to short acceptance lengths and modest speedups. Moving to semantic or segment-level verification can substantially increase acceptance granularity, but prior approaches rely on sequential verification, introducing significant overhead and limiting practical gains. PARSE introduces parallel prefix verification, enabling semantic-level verification without sequential checks. Given a full draft from a draft model, the target model evaluates correctness across multiple prefixes in a single forward pass using a custom attention mask, directly identifying the maximal valid prefix. This eliminates sequential segment verification, and makes verification compute-efficient. PARSE is orthogonal to token-level speculative decoding and can be composed with it for additional gains. Across models and benchmarks, PARSE delivers $1.25\times$ to $4.3\times$ throughput gain over the target model, and $1.6\times$ to $4.5\times$ when composed with EAGLE-3, all with negligible accuracy degradation. This demonstrates parallel prefix verification as an effective, general approach to accelerating LLM inference.

</details>


### [8] [System-of-systems Modeling and Optimization: An Integrated Framework for Intermodal Mobility](https://arxiv.org/abs/2507.08715)
*Paul Saves,Jasper Bussemaker,Rémi Lafage,Thierry Lefebvre,Nathalie Bartoli,Youssef Diouane,Joseph Morlier*

Main category: cs.AI

TL;DR: Surrogate-based optimization (Bayesian optimization with Gaussian processes) helps overcome computational challenges in exploring novel system-of-systems architectures when using dedicated physics-based simulation approaches.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: When developing innovative systems architectures, dedicated physics-based simulation approaches are recommended for system-of-systems to reduce computational complexity. However, exploring novel architectures with these approaches creates challenges for optimization algorithms, including high evaluation costs and potential failures.

Method: The paper proposes using surrogate-based optimization algorithms, specifically Bayesian optimization utilizing Gaussian process models, to address the challenges of architecture exploration with dedicated simulation approaches.

Result: The abstract doesn't present specific results but introduces the methodological approach of using surrogate-based optimization to enable efficient architecture exploration for system-of-systems.

Conclusion: Surrogate-based optimization methods like Bayesian optimization with Gaussian processes provide a viable solution for tackling the computational challenges in novel system-of-systems architecture exploration when using dedicated physics-based simulation approaches.

Abstract: For developing innovative systems architectures, modeling and optimization techniques have been central to frame the architecting process and define the optimization and modeling problems. In this context, for system-of-systems the use of efficient dedicated approaches (often physics-based simulations) is highly recommended to reduce the computational complexity of the targeted applications. However, exploring novel architectures using such dedicated approaches might pose challenges for optimization algorithms, including increased evaluation costs and potential failures. To address these challenges, surrogate-based optimization algorithms, such as Bayesian optimization utilizing Gaussian process models have emerged.

</details>


### [9] [Agent Island: A Saturation- and Contamination-Resistant Benchmark from Multiagent Games](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04312)
*Connacher Murphy*

Main category: cs.AI

TL;DR: Agent Island is a dynamic multiplayer simulation benchmark that addresses saturation and contamination issues in static AI capability evaluation by having language models compete in adaptive social games, with GPT-5.5 emerging as the dominant player.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Static capability benchmarks suffer from saturation (top models reaching ceiling performance) and contamination (models being trained on benchmark data), making it difficult to track true capabilities progress over time.

Method: Created Agent Island, a multiplayer simulation environment where language-model agents compete in social games involving cooperation, conflict, and persuasion. Uses Bayesian Plackett-Luce model to rank players and quantify uncertainty. Conducted 999 games with 49 unique models.

Result: GPT-5.5 dominates with posterior mean skill of 5.64, significantly outperforming GPT-5.2 (3.10) and GPT-5.3-codex (2.86). Models show 8.3 percentage point preference for same-provider finalists, with strongest effect in OpenAI models and weakest in Anthropic models.

Conclusion: Agent Island provides a dynamic benchmark that avoids saturation and contamination by having models compete adaptively against each other. The approach reveals not just model capabilities but also interesting behavioral patterns like provider preferences.

Abstract: Static capabilities benchmarks suffer from saturation and contamination, making it difficult to track capabilities progress over time. We introduce Agent Island, a multiplayer simulation environment in which language-model agents compete in a game of interagent cooperation, conflict, and persuasion. The environment yields a dynamic benchmark designed to mitigate both saturation and contamination; new models can always outperform the current leading player in this winner-take-all game, and agents compete against other adaptive agents rather than face a fixed task set. We rank players with a Bayesian Plackett-Luce model, allowing us to quantify uncertainty in player skill. In 999 games involving 49 unique models, openai/gpt-5.5 dominates its peers with a posterior mean skill of 5.64, compared with 3.10 for the second-ranked model, openai/gpt-5.2, and 2.86 for the third-ranked model, openai/gpt-5.3-codex. We release the game logs as a dataset for analyses of model behavior. As an example, we investigate same-provider preference in final-round votes and find that models are 8.3 p.p. more likely to support a same-provider finalist than finalists from other providers. This preference is not uniform across providers: among separately estimated providers, the effect is strongest for OpenAI models and weakest for Anthropic models.

</details>


### [10] [The Scaling Properties of Implicit Deductive Reasoning in Transformers](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04330)
*Enrico Vompa,Tanel Tammet*

Main category: cs.AI

TL;DR: Depth-bounded Transformers can achieve near-explicit Chain-of-Thought reasoning performance on Horn clause deduction tasks when properly aligned, though CoT remains essential for depth extrapolation.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To understand the scaling properties of implicit deductive reasoning in Transformers, specifically how they handle Horn clause deduction tasks compared to explicit chain-of-thought approaches, and whether implicit reasoning can approach explicit reasoning performance.

Method: Systematically decorrelating provability from spurious features, enforcing algorithmic alignment, testing with depth-bounded Transformers using bidirectional prefix masks across various graph topologies and problem widths.

Result: In sufficiently deep models with bidirectional prefix masks, implicit reasoning approaches explicit CoT performance across different graph topologies and problem widths. However, chain-of-thought reasoning remains necessary for depth extrapolation beyond training distributions.

Conclusion: Implicit reasoning in Transformers can approach explicit CoT performance for deductive reasoning tasks when properly structured, but explicit reasoning mechanisms (CoT) are still required for generalization to deeper reasoning depths than seen during training.

Abstract: We investigate the scaling properties of implicit deductive reasoning over Horn clauses in depth-bounded Transformers. By systematically decorrelating provability from spurious features and enforcing algorithmic alignment, we find that in sufficiently deep models with a bidirectional prefix mask, implicit reasoning approaches explicit CoT performance across graph topologies and problem widths, though CoT remains necessary for depth extrapolation.

</details>


### [11] [When Context Hurts: The Crossover Effect of Knowledge Transfer on Multi-Agent Design Exploration](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04361)
*Saranyan Vigraham*

Main category: cs.AI

TL;DR: Context injection in multi-agent software design shows a crossover effect: same artifact type can improve design exploration on some tasks but degrade it on others, with baseline exploration without context predicting the direction.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Challenge the prevailing assumption that more context is always better for agent orchestration, and investigate whether context injection actually improves multi-agent software design performance across different tasks.

Method: Conducted large-scale experiments with 10 tasks, 7 context-injection conditions, and over 2,700 runs. Measured the effect of different context types (including irrelevant documents) on design exploration. Analyzed correlation with baseline exploration without context. Probed mechanisms by manipulating convergence pressure through prompt design to distinguish natural vs. induced convergence regimes.

Result: Found a crossover effect where the same artifact type could improve design exploration by up to 20× tradeoff coverage on some tasks while reducing it by up to 46% on others. Irrelevant documents sometimes performed as well as or better than relevant artifacts. Baseline exploration without context strongly predicted effect direction (Pearson r = -0.82, p < 0.001). Two distinct convergence regimes: natural convergence (driven by training data priors) responds to artifact disruption, while induced convergence (driven by explicit instructions) does not.

Conclusion: Context injection should be conditional rather than universal. A single no-context trial serves as a cheap diagnostic to predict whether knowledge artifacts will help or hurt a given task, challenging the "more context is always better" assumption in agent orchestration.

Abstract: The prevailing assumption in agent orchestration is that more context is better. We test this on multi-agent software design across 10 tasks, 7 context-injection conditions, and over 2,700 runs, and find a crossover effect: the same artifact type improves design exploration on some tasks (up to 20$\times$ tradeoff coverage) and actively degrades it on others (up to 46% reduction). On several tasks, an irrelevant document performs as well as or better than every relevant artifact. The direction is predicted by a single measurable variable--baseline exploration without context--with Pearson $r = -0.82$ ($p < 0.001$). Probing the mechanism by manipulating convergence pressure through prompt design reveals two distinct regimes: convergence driven by training data priors (natural) responds to artifact disruption, while convergence driven by explicit instructions (induced) does not. The implication is that context injection should be conditional, not universal: one no-context trial is a cheap diagnostic that predicts whether knowledge artifacts will help or hurt a given task.

</details>


### [12] [Deployment-Relevant Alignment Cannot Be Inferred from Model-Level Evaluation Alone](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04454)
*Varad Vishwarupe,Nigel Shadbolt,Marina Jirotka,Ivan Flechais*

Main category: cs.AI

TL;DR: Current alignment evaluation focuses too much on model-level benchmarks; deployment-relevant alignment requires multi-level assessment from model to interaction to deployment, as model-level metrics alone miss crucial interaction dynamics.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Current alignment evaluation relies heavily on model-level benchmarks that assess outputs under fixed inputs (truthfulness, instruction following, preferences), but these are insufficient for understanding alignment in real-world deployment contexts where user interactions and scaffolding matter.

Method: Conducted two studies: 1) Structured audit of 11+ alignment benchmarks using dual-coded eight-dimension rubric (Cohen's kappa=0.87) to analyze verification support and process steerability; 2) Blinded cross-model stress test with 180 transcripts across three frontier models and four scaffolds to examine model-dependent scaffold efficacy.

Result: Benchmark audit found no user-facing verification support and minimal process steerability across all benchmarks; interactional benchmarks (tau-bench, CURATe, Rifts, Common Ground) are fragmented. Stress test showed scaffold efficacy is model-dependent - same scaffold raised one model's verification to ceiling while leaving another unchanged, demonstrating model-level evaluation alone cannot address the gap.

Conclusion: Alignment evaluation needs a system-level approach: alignment profiles instead of single scores, fixed-scaffolding protocols for comparable interactional evaluation, and explicit reporting templates that document the inferential distance between evidence and deployment claims.

Abstract: Alignment evaluation in machine learning has largely become evaluation of models. Influential benchmarks score model outputs under fixed inputs, such as truthfulness, instruction following, or pairwise preference, and these scores are often used to support claims about deployed alignment. This paper argues that deployment-relevant alignment cannot be inferred from model-level evaluation alone. Alignment claims should instead be indexed to the level at which evidence is collected: model-level, response-level, interaction-level, or deployment-level. Two studies support this position. First, a structured audit of eleven alignment benchmarks, extended to a sixteen-benchmark corpus, dual-coded against an eight-dimension rubric with Cohen's kappa = 0.87, finds that user-facing verification support is absent across every benchmark examined, while process steerability is nearly absent. The few interactional benchmarks identified, including tau-bench, CURATe, Rifts, and Common Ground, remain fragmented in coverage, and benchmark construction rather than data source determines what is measured. Second, a blinded cross-model stress test using 180 transcripts across three frontier models and four scaffolds finds that the same verification scaffold raises one model's verification support to ceiling while leaving another categorically unchanged. This shows that scaffold efficacy is model-dependent and that the gap identified by the audit cannot be closed at the model level alone. We propose a system-level evaluation agenda: alignment profiles instead of single scores, fixed-scaffolding protocols for comparable interactional evaluation, and reporting templates that make the inferential distance between evaluation evidence and deployment claims explicit.

</details>


### [13] [How Does Thinking Mode Change LLM Moral Judgments? A Controlled Instant-vs-Thinking Comparison Across Five Frontier Models](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04488)
*Sai Sourabh Madur*

Main category: cs.AI

TL;DR: Provider-exposed reasoning mode doesn't significantly change LLM moral judgments overall, but reduces cross-model disagreement on disputed scenarios and improves consistency with demographic judgments.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: To investigate whether making AI reasoning processes visible (thinking mode) influences moral judgments compared to instant outputs, and how this affects agreement patterns across different frontier LLMs.

Method: Evaluated 100 moral-judgment scenarios across 5 reasoning-trained LLMs (Claude Sonnet 4.6, GPT 5.5, Gemini 3 Flash, DeepSeek V3.1, Qwen3.5 397B). Compared instant vs. thinking modes using Krippendorff's alpha for agreement. Analyzed disputed scenarios separately and examined changes in self-labeled ethical frameworks.

Result: Overall moral judgment agreement remains similar (alpha = 0.78 vs. 0.79). Disagreement concentrates in 21 disputed scenarios where instant-mode agreement is near chance (alpha = 0.08). Reasoning reduces cross-model disagreement on disputed scenarios (increases mean pairwise agreement from 5.4 to 6.7/10). Improves demographic-judgment consistency in 3 of 5 models. Reasoning changes ethical frameworks more often than binary verdicts across all models.

Conclusion: Enabling reasoning mode doesn't substantially alter aggregate moral judgments but improves consistency, particularly on difficult cases where models initially disagree. Revealing AI reasoning processes may enhance alignment without fundamentally changing outputs.

Abstract: We evaluate whether enabling provider-exposed reasoning mode changes moral judgments within the same model checkpoint. Across 100 moral-judgment scenarios and five frontier reasoning-trained LLMs (Claude Sonnet 4.6, GPT 5.5, Gemini 3 Flash, DeepSeek V3.1, and Qwen3.5 397B), aggregate binary-verdict agreement remains high and statistically indistinguishable between instant and thinking modes (Krippendorff's alpha = 0.78 vs. 0.79). However, disagreement is concentrated in 21 model-disputed scenarios, where instant-mode agreement is near chance (alpha = 0.08). On these scenarios, reasoning directionally narrows cross-model disagreement, increasing mean pairwise agreement from 5.4 to 6.7 out of 10. Reasoning also reduces demographic-judgment inconsistency in three of five models and does not increase it for any model. Across all five model families, reasoning changes self-labeled ethical frameworks more often than binary verdicts.

</details>


### [14] [From Parameter Dynamics to Risk Scoring : Quantifying Sample-Level Safety Degradation in LLM Fine-tuning](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04572)
*Xiao Wang,Yifei Zhang,YongKang Liu,Xiaocui Yang,Zihan Wang,Shi Feng,Daling Wang*

Main category: cs.AI

TL;DR: Safety alignment in LLMs is fragile and can be broken by fine-tuning on a small number of benign samples; the paper proposes SQSD to quantify how individual training samples contribute to safety degradation by analyzing parameter drift during fine-tuning.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Safety alignment in Large Language Models is extremely fragile - fine-tuning on just a few benign samples can erase safety behaviors learned from millions of preference examples. Existing studies focus on comparing parameters and hidden states before/after fine-tuning but miss the dynamic evolution during the process.

Method: The paper proposes Sample-Level Quantification of Safety Degradation (SQSD), which quantifies each training sample's influence on safety degradation by measuring the projection difference between danger and safety directions of their induced parameter updates. SQSD computes continuous risk scores to samples based on their parameter drift.

Result: Extensive experiments across multiple models and datasets show that SQSD effectively quantifies sample-level fine-tuning risks and demonstrates strong transferability across different model architectures, parameter scales, and parameter-efficient methods.

Conclusion: The research uncovers that safety degradation occurs through cumulative parameter drift toward danger-aligned directions during fine-tuning, and that samples contributing more to this drift have greater fine-tuning risks. SQSD provides an effective method to quantify these risks at the sample level.

Abstract: Safety alignment of Large Language Models (LLMs) is extremely fragile, as fine-tuning on a small number of benign samples can erase safety behaviors learned from millions of preference examples. Existing studies attempt to explain this phenomenon by comparing parameters and hidden states before and after fine-tuning, but overlook their dynamic evolution during fine-tuning. In this paper, we uncover a critical mechanism underlying safety degradation by analyzing parameter dynamics, where benign fine-tuning causes parameters to cumulatively drift toward danger-aligned directions, progressively undermining the model's safety. This finding suggests that samples contributing more to this drift has greater fine-tuning risks. Based on this insight, we propose a method of Sample-Level Quantification of Safety Degradation (SQSD), which quantifies the influence of each training sample on safety degradation. Specifically, SQSD computes continuous risk scores to samples by measuring their induced parameter updates' projection difference between danger and safety directions. Extensive experiments across multiple models and datasets demonstrate that SQSD effectively quantifies sample-level fine-tuning risks and exhibits strong transferability across model architectures, parameter scales, and parameter-efficient methods.

*Yuelin Hu,Zhenbo Yu,Zhengxue Cheng,Wei Liu,Li Song*

  <summary>Details</summary>

Method: The method involves creating AuditRepairBench, a corpus of 576,000 registered cells with 96,000 executed traces that operationalizes evaluator-channel-blocking ranking instability. It uses a modular screening architecture with four interchangeable implementations: learned influence proxy, rule-based channel-exposure ratio, counterfactual sensitivity proxy, and sparse human-audit proxy. These are combined into a screening posterior that feeds various analysis components.

Result: The approach achieves pooled AUROC of 0.83 on blinded validation, reduces rank displacement by 55-74% (mean 62%) with minimal code changes, and produces AuditRepairBench-Lite, a rule-only configuration that preserves leaderboard ranking (Kendall τ = 0.88) with 24 GPU-hours of computation.

Conclusion: The paper demonstrates that evaluator-channel coupling in agent-repair systems creates significant ranking instability, provides an effective framework for detecting and mitigating this issue, and offers practical tools (AuditRepairBench) that enable fairer leaderboard evaluations with minimal computational overhead.

Abstract: Agent-repair leaderboards reorder under evaluator reconfiguration, and a measurable share of the reordering is produced by methods that consult evaluator-derived signal during internal selection of candidate repairs. We document this failure mode on a public leaderboard and release AuditRepairBench, a paired-execution trace corpus of 576,000 registered cells (96,000 executed) that operationalizes evaluator-channel-blocking ranking instability within a declared observability boundary. A modular screening architecture decides pathway-blocking through four interchangeable implementations, a learned influence proxy, a rule-based channel-exposure ratio that uses no trained model, a counterfactual sensitivity proxy, and a sparse human-audit proxy, combined into a screening posterior that feeds a cell-level flip functional, a set-valued label, a stratified system score, and a set-valued leaderboard. The resource is supported by mechanism-anchored validation on an 80-case source-level channel-surgery subset, an independent-discovery protocol under which two annotator groups separated from the pipeline developers discover coupling patterns blinded to the screening design and the frozen ensemble attains pooled AUROC 0.83 on their 79 cases, implementation robustness, uncertainty propagation that raises 95% coverage from 0.81 to 0.95, and forward transfer with pooled community-evaluator Spearman \r{ho} = 0.65. Screening-guided blinding patches reduce rank displacement by 55--74% (mean 62%) at fewer than 50 lines of code, whereas random channel blinding produces at most 7% reduction and generic retraining at most 13%. AuditRepairBench-Lite, a rule-only configuration on a 12,000-cell subset, preserves the leaderboard at Kendall τ = 0.88 under twenty-four GPU-hours and is the primary release artifact at 42 GB.

### [17] [Budget-aware Auto Optimizer Configurator](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04711)
*Kang Liu,Wei Peng,Jianchen Hu*

Main category: cs.AI

TL;DR: BAOC is a method that reduces GPU memory usage for optimizer states by assigning budget-aware optimizer configurations to different network blocks based on gradient behavior analysis.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Optimizer states consume massive GPU memory in large-scale model training, but gradients in different network blocks exhibit distinct behaviors, making global optimizer configurations memory-inefficient since expensive optimizer states aren't universally necessary.

Method: BAOC samples gradient streams to derive statistical metrics quantifying performance risk of cheaper configurations, then solves a constrained allocation problem to minimize total risk under memory and time budgets, selecting suitable configurations (e.g., low precision or removing momentum) for each block.

Result: Experiments across vision, language, and diffusion workloads show BAOC maintains training quality while significantly reducing memory usage of optimizer states.

Conclusion: BAOC provides an effective approach to reduce memory overhead in large-scale training by budget-aware optimizer configuration allocation based on gradient behavior analysis across network blocks.

Abstract: Optimizer states occupy massive GPU memory in large-scale model training. However, gradients in different network blocks exhibit distinct behaviors, such as varying directional stability and scale anisotropy, implying that expensive optimizer states are not universally necessary and using a global optimizer is often memory-inefficient. We propose the Budget-Aware Optimizer Configurator (BAOC) to reduce memory cost by assigning suitable optimizer configurations to individual blocks under given budgets. Specifically, BAOC samples gradient streams to derive statistical metrics that quantify the potential performance risk of applying cheaper configurations (e.g., low precision or removing momentum). It then solves a constrained allocation problem to minimize total risk under memory and time budgets, selecting a budget-feasible configuration for each block. Experiments across vision, language, and diffusion workloads demonstrate that BAOC maintains training quality while significantly reducing the memory usage of optimizer states. The code is available at https://anonymous.4open.science/r/BAOC-45C6.

System released under AGPL-3.0 with Model Context Protocol server.

A single unsafe action, including accidental deletion, credential exposure, or data exfiltration, can cause irreversible harm. Existing defenses are incomplete: post-hoc benchmarks measure behavior after execution, static guardrails miss obfuscation and multi-step context, and infrastructure sandboxes constrain where code runs without understanding what an action means.
  We present AgentTrust, a runtime safety layer that intercepts agent tool calls before execution and returns a structured verdict: allow, warn, block, or review. AgentTrust combines a shell deobfuscation normalizer, SafeFix suggestions for safer alternatives, RiskChain detection for multi-step attack chains, and a cache-aware LLM-as-Judge for ambiguous inputs.
  We release a 300-scenario benchmark across six risk categories and an additional 630 independently constructed real-world adversarial scenarios. On the internal benchmark, the production-only ruleset achieves 95.0% verdict accuracy and 73.7% risk-level accuracy at low-millisecond end-to-end latency. On the 630-scenario benchmark, evaluated under a patched ruleset and not claimed as zero-shot, AgentTrust achieves 96.7% verdict accuracy, including about 93% on shell-obfuscated payloads. AgentTrust is released under the AGPL-3.0 license and provides a Model Context Protocol server for MCP-compatible agents.

Existing single-agent reinforcement learning (RL) approaches and their multi-agent extensions fail to address these challenges as they do not incorporate other agents in the reasoning process. In this work, we propose Strat-Reasoner, a novel RL-based framework that improves LLMs' strategic reasoning ability in multi-agent games. We introduce a novel recursive reasoning paradigm where an agent's reasoning also integrates other agents' reasoning processes. To provide effective reward signals for the intermediate reasoning sequences, we employ a centralized Chain-of-Thought (CoT) comparison module to evaluate the reasoning quality. ### [23] [A Foundation Model for Zero-Shot Logical Rule Induction](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04916)
*Yin Jun Phua*

Main category: cs.AI

TL;DR: NRI is a pretrained model for zero-shot rule induction in ILP that represents literals using domain-agnostic statistical properties instead of literal identities, enabling generalization across tasks without retraining.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Existing ILP methods are transductive - their learned parameters are bound to specific predicates and require retraining for each new task, limiting practical application.

Method: Uses statistical encoder to represent literals with domain-agnostic properties (class-conditional rates, entropy, co-occurrence). Features parallel slot-based decoder to preserve permutation invariance of logical disjunction, and Product T-norm relaxation to make rule execution differentiable for end-to-end training.

Result: Evaluated on rule recovery, robustness to label noise and spurious correlations, and zero-shot transfer to real-world benchmarks, showing promising performance without task-specific retraining.

Conclusion: NRI opens up the possibility of foundation models for symbolic reasoning by enabling zero-shot rule induction through domain-agnostic statistical representation and parallel decoding architecture.

Abstract: Inductive Logic Programming (ILP) learns interpretable logical rules from data. Existing methods are transductive: their learned parameters are bound to specific predicates and require retraining for each new task. We introduce Neural Rule Inducer (NRI), a pretrained model for zero-shot rule induction. Rather than encoding literal identities, NRI represents literals using domain-agnostic statistical properties such as class-conditional rates, entropy, and co-occurrence, which generalize across variable identities and counts without retraining. The model consists of a statistical encoder and a parallel slot-based decoder. Parallel decoding preserves the permutation invariance of logical disjunction; an autoregressive decoder would instead impose an arbitrary clause order. Product T-norm relaxation makes rule execution differentiable, allowing end-to-end training on prediction accuracy alone. We evaluate NRI on rule recovery, robustness to label noise and spurious correlations, and zero-shot transfer to real-world benchmarks, and we believe this work opens up the possibility of foundation models for symbolic reasoning. Code and the reference checkpoint are available at https://github.com/phuayj/neural-rule-inducer.

### [24] [On-line Learning in Tree MDPs by Treating Policies as Bandit Arms](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04979)
*Anvay Shah,Ramsundar Anandanarayanan,Sharayu Moharir,Shivaram Kalyanakrishnan*

Main category: cs.AI

TL;DR: Online learning algorithms for Tree Markov Decision Problems using bandit techniques with polynomial complexity via shared data confidence bounds.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: T-MDPs arise naturally as abstractions for decision making in sequential games with perfect recall against stationary opponents. The challenge is online learning in T-MDPs where traditional bandit approaches would treat each policy as an arm, but the exponential number of policies makes this computationally infeasible.

Method: Apply bandit algorithms (LUCB and UCB) to T-MDPs by treating each policy as an arm, but design novel confidence bounds based on data shared by policies to enable polynomial memory and per-step computation despite exponential policy count.

Result: Obtain instance-dependent upper bounds on sample complexity and regret that sum a "gap term" from every terminal state rather than every policy. Empirically, the algorithms consistently outperform alternatives on hidden-information games.

Conclusion: The paper presents efficient online learning algorithms for T-MDPs that leverage bandit techniques with innovative confidence bound design to overcome computational challenges, demonstrating both theoretical guarantees and empirical superiority on game benchmarks.

Abstract: A Tree Markov Decision Problem (T-MDP) is a finite-horizon MDP with a starting state $s_{1}$, in which every state is reachable from $s_{1}$ through exactly one state-action trajectory. T-MDPs arise naturally as abstractions of decision making in sequential games with perfect recall, against stationary opponents. We consider the problem of on-line learning in T-MDPs, both in the PAC and the regret-minimisation regimes. We show that well-known bandit algorithms -- \textsc{Lucb} and \textsc{Ucb} -- can be applied on T-MDPs by treating each policy as an arm. The apparent technical challenge in this approach is that the number of policies is exponential in the number of states. Our main innovation is in the design of confidence bounds based on data shared by the policies, so that the bandit algorithms can yet be implemented with polynomial memory and per-step computation. We obtain instance-dependent upper bounds on sample complexity and regret that sum a ``gap term'' from every terminal state, rather than every policy. Empirically, our algorithms consistently outperform available alternatives on a suite of hidden-information games.

### [25] [Uno-Orchestra: Parsimonious Agent Routing via Selective Delegation](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.05007)

Method: Introduced Uno-Orchestra, a unified orchestration policy that selectively decomposes tasks and dispatches subtasks to appropriate (model, primitive) pairs. Both decisions are learned together from curated reinforcement learning trajectories grounded in real worker interactions.

Result: Against 22 baselines on a 13-benchmark suite spanning math, code, knowledge, long-context, and agentic tool-use, Uno-Orchestra reaches 77.0% macro pass@1, roughly 16% above the strongest workflow baseline, at roughly an order of magnitude lower per-query cost.

Abstract: Large language model (LLM) multi-agent systems typically rely on rigid orchestration, committing either to flat per-query routing or to hand-engineered task decomposition, so decomposition depth, worker choice, and inference budget are not jointly optimized under one objective. We introduce Uno-Orchestra, a unified orchestration policy that selectively decomposes a task and dispatches each subtask to an admissible (model, primitive) pair, with both decisions learned together from curated RL trajectories grounded in real worker interactions. Against 22 baselines on a 13-benchmark suite spanning math, code, knowledge, long-context, and agentic tool-use, Uno-Orchestra reaches 77.0% macro pass@1, roughly 16% above the strongest workflow baseline, at roughly an order of magnitude lower per-query cost, advancing the accuracy-efficiency frontier of selective delegation.

SPINE decomposes the EAI pipeline into various stages and establishes a multi-criterion privacy classification matrix to orchestrate contextual sensitivity across stage boundaries. We conduct preliminary simulation and real-world case studies to conceptually validate how privacy constraints propagate downstream to reshape system behavior, illustrating the insufficiency of fragmented privacy patches and motivating future research directions into secure yet functional embodied AI systems. ### [28] [LongSeeker: Elastic Context Orchestration for Long-Horizon Search Agents](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.05191)
*Yijun Lu,Rui Ye,Yuwen Du,Jiajun Wang,Songhua Liu,Siheng Chen*

Main category: cs.AI

  <summary>Details</summary>

Method: Introduces Context-ReAct, a unified agentic paradigm integrating reasoning, context management, and tool use with five atomic operations: Skip, Compress, Rollback, Snippet, and Delete. Develops LongSeeker, a fine-tuned agent from Qwen3-30B-A3B on 10k synthesized trajectories.

Naively accumulating all intermediate content can overwhelm the agent, increasing costs and the risk of errors. We propose that effective context management should be adaptive: parts of the agent's trajectory are maintained at different levels of detail depending on their current relevance to the task. To operationalize this principle, we introduce Context-ReAct, a general agentic paradigm for elastic context orchestration that integrates reasoning, context management, and tool use in a unified loop. Context-ReAct provides five atomic operations: Skip, Compress, Rollback, Snippet and Delete, which allow the agent to dynamically reshape its working context, preserving important evidence, summarizing resolved information, discarding unhelpful branches, and controlling context size. We prove that the Compress operator is expressively complete, while the other specialized operators provide efficiency and fidelity guarantees that reduce generation cost and hallucination risk. Building on this paradigm, we develop LongSeeker, a long-horizon search agent fine-tuned from Qwen3-30B-A3B on 10k synthesized trajectories. Across four representative search benchmarks, LongSeeker achieves 61.5% on BrowseComp and 62.5% on BrowseComp-ZH, substantially outperforming Tongyi DeepResearch (43.2% and 46.7%) and AgentFold (36.2% and 47.3%). These results highlight the potential of adaptive context management, showing that agents can achieve more reliable and efficient long-horizon reasoning by actively shaping their working memory.

Using a minimal dynamical model, we illustrate how this mechanism produces sustained endogenous regime transitions without external scheduling. ### [30] [A Self-Attentive Meta-Optimizer with Group-Adaptive Learning Rates and Weight Decay](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04055)
*JiangBo Zhao,ZhaoXin Liu*

Main category: cs.LG

<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Standard optimizers like AdamW apply uniform hyperparameters across all parameter groups, ignoring heterogeneous optimization dynamics across different layers and modules in deep neural networks.

Method: Proposes MetaAdamW with a lightweight Transformer encoder that extracts statistical features (gradient norms, momentum norms, correlations) from each parameter group and uses self-attention to dynamically modulate per-group learning rates and weight decay. Training uses a meta-learning objective combining gradient alignment, loss decrease, and generalization gap. Introduces extension of homoscedastic uncertainty weighting with task-specific priorities to scale regularization terms.

Result: Extensive experiments on five diverse tasks (time series forecasting, language modeling, machine translation, image classification, sentiment analysis) show MetaAdamW consistently outperforms AdamW baseline in validation loss, accuracy, or perplexity. Achieves up to 17.11% training time reduction or up to 11.08% performance improvement with moderate overhead, while mitigating premature convergence issues.

Conclusion: MetaAdamW successfully addresses the limitation of uniform hyperparameter application by enabling dynamic per-group optimization, demonstrating effectiveness across diverse tasks with improved efficiency and performance.

Abstract: Adaptive optimizers like AdamW apply uniform hyperparameters across all parameter groups, ignoring heterogeneous optimization dynamics across layers and modules. We address this limitation by proposing MetaAdamW - a new optimizer that integrates a self-attention mechanism to dynamically modulate per-group learning rates and weight decay. The modulation factors are produced by a lightweight Transformer encoder that operates on statistical features (gradient norms, momentum norms, correlations) extracted from each parameter group. To train the attention module, we introduce a meta-learning objective that combines gradient alignment, loss decrease, and generalization gap. A key novel contribution is the extension of homoscedastic uncertainty weighting (HUW) with task-specific priorities that directly scale the regularization terms - enabling domain knowledge to guide automatic loss balancing. Extensive experiments on five diverse tasks-time series forecasting (ETT), language modeling (WikiText-2), machine translation (Multi30k), image classification (CIFAR-10), and sentiment analysis (IMDB) - demonstrate that MetaAdamW consistently outperforms the standard AdamW baseline in terms of validation loss, accuracy, or perplexity. Depending on the task, MetaAdamW either reduces overall training time (by up to 17.11%) or improves performance (by up to 11.08%) while introducing only moderate overhead; in some cases, it can also mitigate issues of insufficient convergence caused by premature early stopping. Ablation studies validate the effectiveness of each component, including feature versions, grouping strategies, and the proposed priority-injected uncertainty weighting.

### [31] [Transformation Categorization Based on Group Decomposition Theory Using Parameter Division](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04056)
*Takayuki Komatsu,Yoshiyuki Ohmura,Yasuo Kuniyoshi*

Main category: cs.LG

TL;DR: A group-theoretic approach for unsupervised learning of transformation categories without auxiliary assumptions, using parameter division and homomorphism constraints to decompose transformations into normal subgroups.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Current representation learning lacks principled understanding of what makes representations "good." Classical disentanglement methods fail when factors are coupled, and previous group-theoretic approaches required auxiliary assumptions that weren't necessary according to decomposition theory.

Method: Proposes parameter division for single transformations: split transformation parameters into components, impose homomorphism constraints mapping full transformation to one component, and identify normal subgroup as transformations where that component equals identity. This drops previous auxiliary assumptions like motion and isometry restrictions.

Result: Evaluated on image pairs with rotation, translation, and scale transformations. Ablation studies show that group-decomposition constraints are what drive appropriate categorization, separating theory-based effects from auxiliary assumptions.

Conclusion: The proposed parameter division approach provides a more general group-theoretic framework for unsupervised transformation categorization that aligns with decomposition theory without needing unnecessary auxiliary constraints, enabling principled representation learning for coupled factors.

Abstract: Representation learning seeks meaningful sensory representations without supervision and can model aspects of human development. Although many neural networks empirically learn useful features, a principled account of what makes a representation "good" remains elusive. We study unsupervised categorization of transformations between pairs of inputs under algebraic constraints. Classical disentanglement favors mutually independent factors and fails when factors are coupled. Our prior Galois-theoretic approach decomposes a group via normal subgroups by learning a product of two transformations with one factor constrained to a normal subgroup, covering both commutative and non-commutative cases. That method, however, relied on auxiliary assumptions (e.g., motion and isometry restrictions) not required by decomposition theory, and ablations did not separate theory-based from auxiliary effects. We propose parameter division for a single transformation: we split its parameter into components, impose homomorphism constraints mapping the full transformation to one component, and identify the normal subgroup as the set of transformations when that component is fixed to the identity. This formulation drops the previous auxiliary assumptions and applies more broadly. We evaluate on image pairs involving rotation, translation, and scale; ablations show that group-decomposition constraints drive appropriate categorization.

Large language models (LLMs) are a promising assistant for NAS because they can translate rich architectural and coding priors into executable code edits. However, in practice, seemingly local revisions often propagate into non-local behavioral and performance shifts because a single edit can inadvertently couple multiple interacting functional factors, a phenomenon we refer to as functional entanglement. To make LLM knowledge usable under such entanglement, we propose Structured Progressive Knowledge Activation (SPARK), which activates relevant priors by explicitly selecting the functional factor to modify and conditioning the edit on that factor. This factor-conditioned editing reduces entangled side effects and yields more targeted, reliable architecture modifications. On CLRS-DFS, SPARK achieves a 28.1x sample-efficient architecture evolution speedup and yields a 22.9 percent relative improvement in OOD accuracy.

To address these limitations, we propose a novel Mixed-Precision Interactive Side Mixture-of-Experts framework (MP-ISMoE). Specifically, we first propose a Gaussian Noise Perturbed Iterative Quantization (GNP-IQ) scheme to quantize weights into lower-bits while effectively decreasing quantization errors. By leveraging memory conserved from GNP-IQ, we subsequently employ Interactive Side Mixture-of-Experts (ISMoE) to scaling up side networks without sacrificing overall memory efficiency. Different from conventional mixture-of-experts, ISMoE learns to select optimal experts by interacting with salient features from frozen backbones, thus suppressing knowledge forgetting and boosting performance. Extensive experiments across diverse vision-language and language-only tasks demonstrate that MP-ISMoE remarkably promotes accuracy compared to state-of-the-art METL approaches, while maintaining comparable parameter and memory efficiency.

### [34] [Continual Distillation of Teachers from Different Domains](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04059)

  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: Deep learning models are scaling to sizes that require more storage than many datasets, necessitating new approaches for knowledge transfer that don't require storing previous models or their training data.

Method: Proposes Self External Data Distillation (SE2D), which preserves logits on external unlabeled data to stabilize learning across heterogeneous teachers in the continual distillation framework, addressing Unseen Knowledge Forgetting.

Result: Experiments on multiple benchmarks show that SE2D reduces Unseen Knowledge Forgetting (UKF) and improves cross-domain generalization compared to baseline approaches.

Abstract: Deep learning models continue to scale, with some requiring more storage than many large-scale datasets. Thus, we introduce a new paradigm: Continual Distillation (CD), where a student learns sequentially from a stream of teacher models without retaining access to earlier teachers. CD faces two challenges: teacher training data is unavailable, and teachers have varying expertise. We show that external unlabeled data enables Unseen Knowledge Transfer (UKT), allowing the student to acquire information from domains not present in the training data, while known to the teacher. We also show that sequential distillation causes Unseen Knowledge Forgetting (UKF) when transferred knowledge is lost after training on later teachers. To better trade off between UKT and UKF, we propose Self External Data Distillation (SE2D), a method that preserves logits on external data to stabilize learning across heterogeneous teachers. Experiments on multiple benchmarks show that SE2D reduces UKF and improves cross-domain generalization. The code and implementation for this work are publicly available at: https://github.com/Nicolas1203/continual_distillation.

### [35] [Lookahead Drifting Model](https://arxiv.org/abs/2605.04060)
*Guoqiang Zhang,Kenta Niwa,W. Bastiaan Kleijn*

Main category: cs.LG

TL;DR: A lookahead drifting model that computes sequential drifting terms at each training iteration, using previous terms to capture higher-order gradient information for improved distribution mapping.


<details>
  <summary>Details</summary>
Motivation: The drifting model paradigm has achieved state-of-the-art image generation performance on ImageNet with one-step neural functional evaluation, but there's potential to improve by capturing more complex gradient information during training.

Method: Proposes a lookahead drifting model that computes multiple drifting terms sequentially at each training iteration. Each drifting term uses previously computed terms, positive samples, and model outputs. The terms capture higher-order gradient information, with later terms capturing more complex information. The model is optimized by pushing outputs toward a weighted summation of these drifting terms.

Result: Experimental results on toy examples and CIFAR10 demonstrate better performance than baseline drifting models, showing improved distribution mapping capabilities.

Conclusion: The lookahead drifting model effectively improves upon existing drifting models by incorporating sequential, higher-order gradient information through multiple drifting terms, leading to better performance in distribution mapping tasks.

Abstract: Recently, a new paradigm named \emph{drifting model} has been proposed for mapping distributions, which achieves the SOTA image generation performance over ImageNet via one-step neural functional evaluation (NFE). The basic idea is to compute a drifting term at each training iteration and then push the output of the model towards the direction of the drifting term. In this paper, we propose a \emph{lookahead drifting model}. At each training iteration, we compute a set of drifting terms sequentially. Each drifting term is calculated by making use of previously computed ones as well as the positive samples and the output of the model. %One key step is to properly scale the drifting terms so that their magnitudes are in a comparable range. In principle, the drifting terms obtained at a later stage capture higher order gradient information towards the positive samples. At each training iteration, the model is optimized by pushing its output towards the direction of the (weighted) summation of the drifting terms. Experimental results on toy examples and CIFAR10 demonstrate the better performance of the new method than the baseline.
